{"category": "Technology", "url": "https://www.eff.org/press/releases/eff-urges-pennsylvania-supreme-court-find-keyword-search-warrant-unconstitutional", "pagename": "EFF Urges Pennsylvania Supreme Court to Find Keyword Search Warrant Unconstitutional ", "date": "2024-01-17", "summary": "The Electronic Frontier Foundation (EFF) and other organizations argue that keyword warrants used by the police to search through search engine databases are unconstitutional and violate privacy rights. These warrants target free speech, lack probable cause, and can implicate innocent people. The case at hand involves a massive invasion of Google users' privacy and sets a dangerous precedent that could be applied to any search engine user. The EFF, along with other groups, filed a brief challenging the constitutionality of these warrants, highlighting their incompatibility with privacy and freedom of speech. The warrants allow police to access users' most private thoughts and opinions without targeting specific individuals or accounts. It is argued that these warrants violate both the Pennsylvania Constitution and the Fourth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. They also pose a threat to protected speech and the right to receive information. The EFF emphasizes the importance of anonymous and unrestricted use of search engines for a free society and warns that dragnet warrants will deter users from seeking information on certain topics."}

Current watermarking schemes can be easily removed and future schemes may face similar issues. Watermarking digital images with visible text is slightly more effective but still not foolproof. Using metadata and cryptographic signatures to prove the authenticity of camera-generated images is a more feasible method. Watermarking text-based AI content is challenging due to rewording. Watermark detection tools can either aid in removing watermarks or hinder the process if kept secret. AI image generators raise concerns for artists, and AI may assist law enforcement in the future."}

{"category": "Technology", "url": "https://www.eff.org/deeplinks/2023/12/taking-back-web-decentralization-2023-review", "pagename": "Taking Back the Web with Decentralization: 2023 in Review", "date": "2024-01-17", "summary": "The internet is witnessing a swing towards decentralization as users push back against the concentration of power and violation of privacy and free expression on major social media platforms. This movement is seen in the growth of new social media projects such as Mastodon and Bluesky. Meta's launch of Threads, a microblogging site using the federated ActivityPub protocol, also contributed to the decentralization trend. The federation of social news aggregation has also gained traction as users turn to alternatives like Lemmy and Kbin in response to changes in platforms like Reddit. The sustainability and safeguarding of these decentralized projects against government overreach remain challenges. There is ongoing work on protocols and libraries that enable decentralized services, such as Veilid and Spritely, promising secure and private data exchange. The European Union's Digital Markets Act and the More Instant Messaging Interoperability working group are pushing for open interoperability and end-to-end encryption in messaging platforms. The DWeb Camp and EFF's testimony on blockchain highlight the importance of policy discussions and exploration in the decentralized web space. Content moderation in decentralized social media is a complex issue being addressed by initiatives like the Task Force for a Trustworthy Future Web. Overall, the decentralization movement is gaining momentum with the exploration of alternatives, the development of protocols, and policy discussions shaping its future."}

{"category": "Technology", "url": "https://techpolicy.press/an-fda-for-ai", "pagename": "An FDA for AI?", "date": "2024-01-17", "summary": "The FDA's regulatory model is being considered as a potential framework for governing AI systems. However, applying the FDA model to AI raises several challenges due to the differences between the two domains. The FDA has a long history of overseeing novel and high-risk technologies, which can serve as inspiration for AI governance. FDA-style approval and oversight would involve risk and novelty-driven oversight, continuous engagement with developers, wide-ranging information access, burden of proof on developers, and a balance between innovation and safety. The FDA model's cost of compliance and limitations are acknowledged, but adjustments can be made to reduce costs while ensuring risk reduction. It is important to consider other regulatory agencies, such as the FAA and NHTSA, for their expertise in specific sectors. International cooperation and standard-setting could also play a role in AI governance, with mutual acceptance of regulatory approvals across jurisdictions. The EU's AI Act has some elements that align with the FDA model, such as a co-developed code of practice for safety and efficacy. Overall, there is a need to find regulatory approaches that address the unique risks and challenges posed by AI technologies."}

{"category": "Technology", "url": "https://www.eff.org/deeplinks/2023/12/great-interoperability-convergence-2023-year-review", "pagename": "The Great Interoperability Convergence: 2023 Year in Review", "date": "2024-01-17", "summary": "Regulators worldwide are converging on solutions to tackle Big Tech dominance and promote user choice and protection. The current approach of making tech platforms responsible for policing their users has failed. Interoperability and smaller platforms offer relief and protection for users. Recent developments include the Digital Markets Act in Europe, the AMERICA Act in the US, and the Digital Markets, Competition, and Consumers Bill in the UK. {"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.09221", "pagename": "Multiple Subset Problem as an encryption scheme for communication. (arXiv:2401.09221v1 [cs.CR])", "date": "2024-01-17", "summary": "Encryption using well-known mathematical problems like the subset sum problem (SSP) is popular for its computational difficulty and security. The multiple-subset problem (MSSP) is a variant of SSP that involves distributing items among bins to maximize total weight without exceeding bin capacity. We introduce a new problem where the sum of subsets from a set of sets must equal a specific integer. This problem is NP-complete but can be efficiently solved for known private keys using an algorithm that discards irrelevant sums. We present an encryption scheme based on MSSP, highlighting its unique applications in communication."}

{"category": "AI", "url": "https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/rz7LkbgnFk6pudmTB/against-the-burden-of-knowledge", "pagename": "Against the Burden of Knowledge", "date": "2024-01-21", "summary": "Key Ideas:\n- The burden of knowledge claims that new ideas get harder to find because more time is spent learning old ones, causing a drag on innovation.\n- There is empirical evidence supporting the burden of knowledge, such as increasing average age of authors and larger research teams.\n- However, examples from history show that past knowledge is often supplanted by new discoveries, decreasing the necessary educational investment.\n- Specialization is a response to an increased burden of knowledge but does not necessarily hinder innovation.\n- Institutional decay in academia could also explain the observed trends of aging researchers and narrower fields.\n- Redesigning academic institutions through metascience could potentially reverse these trends.\n- The burden of knowledge is an intuitive explanation, but it may not explain the divergence between R&D inputs and productivity growth outputs."}

The case at hand involves a keyword search warrant issued to Google, raising concerns about invasion of privacy. If upheld, the ruling could set a precedent for applying these warrants to any search engine user. The EFF argues that keyword search warrants are incompatible with constitutional protections and can implicate innocent individuals. These warrants require providers to search their entire databases for specific keywords, posing serious privacy concerns. The EFF likens them to 18th-century writs of assistance, conducting exploratory searches. They also argue keyword warrants are harmful as they target protected speech and the right to access information, impacting a free society. The NACDL supports the argument, emphasizing the violation of privacy rights. {"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2310.00933", "pagename": "Case Study: Securing MMU-less Linux Using CHERI. (arXiv:2310.00933v2 [cs.OS] UPDATED)", "date": "2024-01-21", "summary": "Key ideas:\n1. MMU-less Linux lacks security due to the lack of protection and isolation mechanisms.\n2. CHERI is used to secure the existing MMU-less Linux version of the RISC-V port by providing complete pointer and memory safety.\n3. CHERI offers significant security guarantees for high-end dynamic MMU-less embedded systems at lower costs compared to MMUs and MPUs.\n4. The software stack is built in pure-capability CHERI C mode for spatial memory safety.\n5. User programs are isolated as separate ELFs, each with its own CHERI-based capability table.\n6. User programs and the kernel are isolated from each other using separate capability tables.\n7. CompartOS' linkage-based compartmentalization is used to compartmentalize kernel modules.\n8. This approach offers a new security front that is not possible with MMU-based Linux, preventing vulnerable/malicious kernel modules from compromising the entire system.\n9. However, regulating RISC-V is legally challenging and may be counterproductive. The recent export controls target AI chips but not general computing processors, so RISC-V doesn't currently pose a threat. However, in the future, if export controls expand to include general-purpose chips, RISC-V could undermine their effectiveness. The U.S. government could try to control China's access to RISC-V technology, but it's difficult due to its international operation. Another approach could be to support the development and adoption of RISC-V to mitigate the threat and encourage innovation at home."}

The \"safety-impacting AI\" category includes broad purposes, potentially discouraging new technology adoption. The \"rights-impacting AI\" qualification is too broad and may classify most AI systems as high risk, making it difficult for agencies to adopt AI tools. A more precise and risk-based approach, like the EU AI Act, is recommended, clarifying definitions and focusing on consequential decisions. Regulatory scope should be based on existing laws, and certain use cases, like determining eligibility for government programs, should have greater scrutiny."}

In this study, researchers developed a natural language processing (NLP) tool to identify problematic opioid use from clinical notes. They compared the characteristics of patients identified through NLP to those identified through ICD codes. NLP exclusively identified a large number of patients, and those identified were more likely to be women. Patients identified through ICD codes were more likely to be male, younger, have concurrent benzodiazepine prescriptions, more comorbidities, more care encounters, and less likely to be married. {"category": "AI", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.13262", "pagename": "Designing Redistribution Mechanisms for Reducing Transaction Fees in Blockchains. High demand and limited resources have led to high fees. Transaction Fee Redistribution Mechanisms (TFRMs) aim to reduce fees by redistributing payments collected from TFMs. The challenge is ensuring allocative efficiency and user incentive compatibility. {"category": "AI", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.13270", "pagename": "Audio-Infused Automatic Image Colorization by Exploiting Audio Scene Semantics. This paper proposes a novel approach that uses corresponding audio to enhance the semantic understanding of grayscale scenes. The proposed network, called AIAIC, consists of three stages: pretraining the network with color image semantics, learning the color semantic correlations between audio and visual scenes, and utilizing the implicit audio semantic representation for colorization. The entire process is self-supervised and does not require human annotation. Experimental results show that audio guidance significantly improves the performance of automatic colorization, particularly for scenes that are difficult to understand from visual modality alone."}

While copyright protection expires, trademark protection lasts indefinitely as long as the mark is still being used. Former copyright holders often use trademark law to maintain control over their works even after they enter the public domain. Disney, for example, has registered a trademark for \"Walt Disney Animation Studios\" which incorporates a snippet from the public domain cartoon Steamboat Willie. However, trademark protection is more limited than copyright and cannot be used to control the distribution of creative works."}

SIM swap and port-out fraud involve fraudsters taking control of a victim's phone number by convincing the carrier to transfer the victim's service to the fraudster's phone. EPIC called for the harmonization of CPNI and CPI rules with SIM swap authentication requirements, additional authentication measures, and mandatory reporting of fraud incidents by carriers. {"category": "Technology", "url": "https://techpolicy.press/evaluating-social-medias-role-in-the-israel-hamas-war", "pagename": "Evaluating Social Media's Role in the Israel-Hamas War", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "Article Title: AI Breakthroughs: The Future of Artificial Intelligence\n\nIntroduction:\nArtificial Intelligence (AI) has experienced numerous breakthroughs in recent years, greatly influencing various industries. From healthcare to finance, AI is being harnessed to solve complex problems and improve efficiency. This article explores some of the key advances in AI and its potential impact on the future.\n\nContent:\n\n1. Deep Learning and Neural Networks:\nDeep learning, a subset of machine learning, has revolutionized AI. It involves training artificial neural networks with vast amounts of data to recognize patterns and make predictions. These networks can \"learn\" from the data, improving performance over time. Deep learning has been applied successfully in image and speech recognition, natural language processing, and even autonomous vehicles.\n\n2. Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs):\nGANs are a type of AI model consisting of a generator and a discriminator network. The generator creates new data instances, such as images, while the discriminator tries to distinguish between real and generated data. Through continuous interaction, GANs have achieved remarkable results in creating realistic images and videos, even mimicking human art styles.\n\n3. Reinforcement Learning:\nReinforcement learning enables AI systems to learn optimal actions through trial and error. By rewarding correct behaviors and penalizing mistakes, AI agents can learn to navigate complex environments and achieve specific goals. Applications of reinforcement learning include robotics, gaming, and autonomous systems.\n\n4. Explainable AI:\nAs AI becomes increasingly sophisticated, there is a growing need for transparency and explainability. Explainable AI aims to provide insights into how AI systems make decisions, enabling humans to understand and trust the algorithms. This is particularly important in sensitive domains like healthcare and finance, where accountability and ethical considerations are crucial.\n\n5. Edge AI and IoT:\nEdge AI refers to AI algorithms running on edge devices, such as smartphones or IoT devices, rather than relying on cloud-based processing. This enables faster, more efficient AI applications, as data processing occurs locally. Edge AI is particularly useful in real-time applications, such as autonomous vehicles or smart home devices.\n\n6. Quantum Computing and AI:\nQuantum computing holds promise for accelerating AI developments through its ability to process vast amounts of data simultaneously. Quantum machine learning algorithms are being explored to enhance AI capabilities and solve complex problems more efficiently. Though still in its early stages, the intersection of quantum computing and AI could lead to game-changing advancements.\n\nKey Ideas Summarized:\n\n- AI breakthroughs like deep learning and neural networks have revolutionized various industries, from healthcare to autonomous vehicles.\n- Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs) have achieved impressive results in creating realistic images and videos.\n- Reinforcement learning enables AI systems to learn optimal actions through trial and error, benefiting areas such as robotics and gaming.\n- Explainable AI is crucial for transparency and accountability, particularly in sensitive domains like healthcare and finance.\n- Edge AI allows for faster and more efficient AI applications by running algorithms on local devices.\n- Quantum computing has the potential to accelerate AI developments and solve complex problems more efficiently when combined with machine learning algorithms."}
{"category": "Technology", "url": "https://www.eff.org/press/releases/eff-urges-pennsylvania-supreme-court-find-keyword-search-warrant-unconstitutional", "pagename": "EFF Urges Pennsylvania Supreme Court to Find Keyword Search Warrant Unconstitutional ", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "Keyword search warrants, which allow police to search through search engine databases, are unconstitutional and violate privacy and free speech rights, according to the Electronic Frontier Foundation (EFF) and other organizations. In a brief filed to the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania, the EFF argues that these warrants lack probable cause and target innocent people. The case in question involves a search warrant issued to Google, but if upheld, it could be applied to any search engine user. The EFF asserts that keyword search warrants are incompatible with constitutional protections and have no place in a democratic society. These warrants are concerning because they do not target specific individuals, but instead require the search of an entire database based on keywords specified by the police. The EFF argues that these warrants violate constitutional rights and harm protected speech and the right to receive information. They also argue that these warrants could have a chilling effect on users seeking out information, as they may fear their searches being monitored by the police. Overall, the EFF and other organizations are urging the Pennsylvania Supreme Court to find keyword search warrants unconstitutional."}

{"category": "Privacy", "url": "https://www.luizasnewsletter.com/p/what-ive-been-reading-november", "pagename": "What I've been reading - November", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "Title: The Promises and Perils of Artificial Intelligence\n\nWith the rapid advancement of technology, artificial intelligence (AI) has become a topic of great interest and concern. AI, the ability of machines to imitate human intelligence and perform tasks that typically require human intelligence, holds enormous potential but also poses significant challenges.\n\nOne of the key promises of AI is its potential to revolutionize various industries and improve our daily lives. For example, AI-powered algorithms can analyze vast amounts of data to provide valuable insights and predictions in fields such as healthcare, finance, and transportation. With AI, doctors can diagnose diseases more accurately, financial institutions can detect fraud more effectively, and self-driving cars can navigate roads more safely.\n\nHowever, along with these promises come potential perils. One major concern is the ethical implications of AI. As AI systems become more sophisticated, they may make decisions that have unintended consequences or exhibit biased behavior. This raises questions about who is accountable for the outcomes generated by AI algorithms and how to ensure fairness and transparency in their decision-making processes.\n\nAnother challenge is the impact of AI on the job market. While AI can automate repetitive and mundane tasks, it also raises concerns about potential job displacement. As machines become more capable, some jobs may no longer require human involvement, leading to unemployment and economic inequality. The challenge lies in finding ways to harness the benefits of AI while mitigating its negative impact on employment.\n\nAdditionally, privacy and security are significant concerns in the age of AI. As AI systems collect and analyze vast amounts of personal data, there is a risk of data breaches and unauthorized access. Safeguarding individuals' privacy and developing robust security measures are crucial to prevent misuse of personal information and protect against cyber threats.\n\nIn conclusion, AI holds considerable promise in transforming various industries and enhancing our lives. However, it also presents significant challenges, including ethical considerations, job displacement, and privacy concerns. Addressing these challenges will require careful planning, collaboration between policymakers and industry leaders, and the development of comprehensive regulations and guidelines to ensure the responsible and beneficial use of AI technology.\n\nKey ideas:\n- AI has the potential to revolutionize industries and improve daily lives.\n- Ethical implications, such as transparency and accountability, need to be addressed.\n- The impact of AI on the job market and potential unemployment should be considered.\n- Privacy and security measures are crucial in the age of AI."}

{"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.13262", "pagename": "Designing Redistribution Mechanisms for Reducing Transaction Fees in Blockchains. (arXiv:2401.13262v1 [cs.GT])", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "Blockchains use Transaction Fee Mechanisms (TFMs) to determine transaction fees. High demand and limited resources have led to high fees. Transaction Fee Redistribution Mechanisms (TFRMs) aim to reduce fees by redistributing collected payments. It is challenging to apply TFRMs due to unconfirmed transactions and strategic manipulation. The proposed \\emph{Robust} TFRM (\\textsf{R-TFRM}) compromises miner rationality to guarantee rebates. {"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.12391", "pagename": "Approximation of Pufferfish Privacy for Gaussian Priors. (arXiv:2401.12391v1 [cs.IT])", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "This paper discusses the approximation of pufferfish privacy when the adversary's belief of published data is Gaussian distributed. The use of Monge's optimal transport plan allows for the achievement of $(\u03b5, \u03b4)$-pufferfish privacy by calibrating additive Laplace noise to the differences in mean and variance of the conditioned Gaussian distributions. The method is applicable to private summation or average queries, with sufficient conditions provided for approximating $\u03b5$-statistical indistinguishability in sensitive data. The approach is further extended to arbitrary prior beliefs trained by Gaussian mixture models, achieving $(\u03b5,\u03b4)$-pufferfish privacy by calibrating noise to a convex combination of mean and variance differences between Gaussian components."}

{"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.12443", "pagename": "Patch2QL: Discover Cognate Defects in Open Source Software Supply Chain With Auto-generated Static Analysis Rules. {"category": "Cybersecurity", "url": "http://arxiv.org/abs/2401.12542", "pagename": "Multi-Party Private Set Intersection: A Circuit-Based Protocol with Jaccard Similarity for Secure and Efficient Anomaly Detection in Network Traffic. (arXiv:2401.12542v1 [cs.CR])", "date": "2024-01-25", "summary": "We present a circuit-based protocol for multi-party private set intersection (PSI) that allows m parties to compute the intersection of their datasets without revealing additional information. Our protocol builds upon the two-party Sort-Compare-Shuffle (SCS) protocol and exhibits acceptable performance. It completes in just 19 seconds with 7 parties and set sizes of 2^12. Circuit-based protocols like ours have an advantage over custom protocols for more complex computation. We showcase this advantage by incorporating a module for calculating the Jaccard similarity metric, which can be used in network traffic analysis for anomaly detection. Our protocol is versatile and preserves privacy while efficiently identifying abnormal patterns in network flow."}
